## Are We Part of the Drama of This World? | Sri Chanchalapathi Dasa | SB 2.5.26-29 | 19.07.2024
**Speaker:** HG Chanchalapathi Dasa

### creation, elements, transformation
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/D1giBxi2ovc?t=0
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "And water being transformed from all life on Earth appears knew in order and as previously becomes qualitatively full of juice, touch, sound and form respectively."
**Summary:** The speaker reads verses from Srimad Bhagavatam describing the transformation of elements in the process of creation.

Om Namo Bhagavate Vasudevaya. Reading from Srimad Bhagavatam, Canto 2, Chapter 5, Verse 26-29. I will read myself. Reading from Srimad Bhagavatam, Canto 2, Chapter 5, Verse 26-29. Translation and purport by His Divine Grace A.C. Bhaktivedanta Swami Srila Prabhupada: "Because the star is transformed, the air is generated with the quality of touch. And by previous succession, the air is also full of sound and the basic principle of duration of life, sense perception, mental power, and bodily strength. When the air is transformed in course of time and nature's course, fire is generated, taking shape with the sense of touch and sound. Since fire is also transformed, there is a manifestation of water full of juice and taste. As previously, it also has form and touch and is also full of sound. And water being transformed from all life on Earth appears anew in order and as previously becomes qualitatively full of juice, touch, sound and form respectively."

### drama of life, roles, creator
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/D1giBxi2ovc?t=447
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** analogy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers, Newcomers
**Key Quote:** "So in the same way Lord Brahma who is the director of this universe creator of the universe he is doing the set design"
**Summary:** The speaker uses the analogy of a film director to explain how Lord Brahma creates the universe and assigns roles to living entities.

Suppose, let's say I'm a film director and I'm planning a film, and in that film I want some of you to become the king, some of you to become the queen, some of you to become warriors, some of you to become an invader, a villain who will come and do all nonsense, all wrong things, and some of you soldiers. And so now, in filmmaking, there is one important step after the script, casting, all that is done, that's called set design. Because it's a story of a king, queen, all this, we need a palace, we need a battleground, we need horses, we need elephants, we need soldiers. Next, as a film director, I'll start planning all of this so that when we turn on the lights and all of you can act out very correctly, the king will play his role, the queen will play her role, and then the invader will come and all the different things will, as per the story, will unfold. So in the same way, Lord Brahma, who is the director of this universe, creator of the universe, he is doing the set design.

### purpose of life, illusion, detachment

**Summary:** The speaker raises the fundamental question of why we are part of this worldly drama and emphasizes that people are usually too engrossed in their roles to contemplate the deeper meaning.

So a fundamental question is, why are we all part of this drama? But this is like a, this, okay, that's like a drama, cinema is all right, but this looks like real life. This doesn't look like drama. No, actually it is a fact. What is a drama, what is a cinema? After some time, the curtains will close and the lights are turned off and the drama ends. So even in our lives, one day the curtain will be drawn, the lights will be turned off, our drama will end, but it doesn't appear like that. It looks like real, you know, this is my wife, this is my husband, this is my home, this is my father, this is my mother, these are my children, this is my house. Why all of this has come about? These are deeper questions. One is, you are a king, play properly your role as a king. You, queen, play properly queen as a role as a queen, do your proper, be a strong king, all that is one thing. But a very fundamental, deeper question is, why have I become an actor in this drama? But very rarely people think, they are all busy with their roles, they have to play mother, father, husband, wife, and they want to play it out nicely so that everybody is impressed with the role I am playing. We rarely think why this drama is going on.

As an Amsha, we are all spirit soul, Amsha of Krishna. Just like there is sunlight. Now can the sun, sunshine, sunlight, is it possible for the sunlight to be independent of the sun? Can sunlight exist without the sun? Not possible at all, isn't it? Constitutionally, it is not possible. The sunlight is an emanation of the sun. In the same way, we are all living entities. We are all conscious entities coming from Krishna. We are all living entities. We are all conscious entities coming from Krishna. We are all living entities. We are all conscious entities coming from Krishna. We are all conscious entities coming from Krishna. But, this conscious entities have developed one desire. Sunshine has no desire. It is just light energy. Whereas, we are also energy, Jeeva Shakti of the Lord. And this Jeeva Shakti has developed a desire, I want to be independent of Krishna. I want to be independent of Krishna.

### illusion, unconstitutional desire, dream
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/D1giBxi2ovc?t=1074
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "This desire of the living entity to be independent of Krishna is called unconstitutional desire."
**Summary:** The speaker elaborates on the unconstitutional desire to be independent of Krishna, comparing it to a dream where sunlight can exist without the sun, and how Krishna creates the illusion of the material world to facilitate this desire.

I want to be independent of Krishna. I want to be independent of Krishna. Krishna. Just like sunlight has come from sun, we are also Jeeva Shakti coming from Krishna, the Shaktimaan. But the difference is that is a inert, lifeless energy, light energy, heat energy. Whereas we are a Shakti which has got Chetana, consciousness. And this Chetana Shakti, Chit Shakti has developed a desire because it's Chetana. Chetana means has desire, has thinking, feeling. And this Chit Shakti has developed a desire, I must be independent of Krishna. It is not possible. Sunshine cannot be independent of the sun. It is an emanation of the sun. This desire of the living entity to be independent of Krishna is called unconstitutional desire. It is not constitutional. It is not by our makeup. How we are composed, how we are formed, what are we made of? We are made of Krishna's energy. We have come from Krishna. So we can never sever that. But we have developed a desire. I want to be independent of Krishna. This is possible only in illusion. For example, we can think of sunshine without sun in our dream. We can say last night I had a dream, you know, there was so much sunlight. I looked up at the sky and I didn't see the sun at all. But there was sunshine. Yes, such a thing is possible in illusory dream. Dream will go away. It's a temporary existence in the night. And when we wake up, it's all gone. Right? In the same way, Krishna through Brahma creates an illusion of this world for the living entities to give an impression that we are independent of Krishna.

That's what we pursue. We have our plans. We get inputs from the society, from newspapers, from the heroes of the world, from different sources. And we form our ambitions and we have to do that. And we want to pursue. These are my desires, my ambition. Rarely we think, if I am part and parcel of Krishna, I have come from Krishna, what was Krishna's plan for me? In the first stage, where we recognize God, I have my independent desires, I have my independent plans. I want God's blessing so that I can succeed in my own plan.

This is also recognition of God, but a relatively very minimal recognition. God as a supplier of my dreams, as a fulfiller of my dreams. My dreams. It's my dream. And God shall kindly fulfill my dreams. See, this is the large population of the world, in every religion. This is the consciousness of the living entity. The next level Krishna teaches in the Bhagavad Gita, in the Vedic literatures, is that, if you are part and parcel of me, Krishna. We are all part and parcel of Krishna. We have come from Krishna. We are an energy of Krishna. What does Krishna want me to do? What is his plan for me? If I am his. If I am his. If I am his. So, this is how Bhagavad Gita ends, by bringing the concept of Sarva-Dharman-Paridhyajya. Ma mekam sharanam vraja. We must surrender to Krishna. We must align our desires, our plans, our activities, with Krishna's activity.

And then what happens? Then, Bhagavatam describes further, after sharanagati, after you align, you will come to understand, you have a relation with Krishna. Relation. Relation is a very powerful thing. Just like somebody is a mother, there is a child. The mother is always conscious, I should take care of my child. And child also, playing around a little bit, if some difficulty, some danger comes, mummy, she will run to the mother, and hold on to the mother. That's the meaning of relationship. One crore rupees in the bank now. The alarm rings, and then I wake up. Will I run to the bank? Let me draw the one crore rupees. No. It's a dream. It has no substance. Same thing will happen to us, when our life's alarm rings, and we go out of this world. Where is all this relationship? Where is my house? Everything is gone.

So, Bhagavatam is preparing us to understand all this and describing here how Brahma created all these sets in the form of the body, in the form of the dress for the body, in the form of the palace, in the form of the houses, and in modern world, in the form of my factory, my shop, my bank, my bank balance, my car. All these different things have come about. That's why, it is very nicely described here in this verse. Sohankara iti prokto vikurvan samabhut tridha. This ahankara, the false identity the living entity wants to take up. The living entity has desire to be independent. Now Lord has to fulfill that. It is not possible to fulfill that. Because it is an unconstitutional desire. It can only be fulfilled in a dreamlike situation. That is why, Srila Prabhupada gives another example of an unconstitutional desire. There was a child. Child, you know children, they become cranky sometimes. They cry, cry so much. They are small children. And the mother is trying to pacify the child, put the child to sleep. Not able to do anything. So when such things happen, you know, in homes, the mother brought the child, you know, sometimes due to heat also, the children go cranky. So she brought the child out of the house in the night. And hoping that, you know, cool, little cool breeze, child will become alright. The child was still very cranky. And now the child looked at the sky and there was the moon. And now the child started demanding, get me the moon. I want the moon. So the mother is very perplexed. What is this? How can I get the moon? Moon is in the sky. The child's desire is an unconstitutional desire. It is not possible for the child to get the moon from the sky. Impossible. It is not in line with the composition and what the child is made of, what the moon is made of.

But the child has developed a desire. The father was an intelligent man. He was watching all this, how the wife, mother is struggling with the child and the child demanding the moon. The father, what he did, he went and brought one big mirror. He said, I want the moon. And the child saw the reflection of the moon in the mirror. And the child saw, oh, the moon is there. And the child was holding the mirror and the child became satisfied. Now I got the moon. Actually the child did not get the moon, got a reflection of the moon. We are related to Krishna, we are meant to have a serving relationship with Krishna but we have developed a desire, I want to be independent, I want to enjoy, I have my plans, I want to have nice relationship in the material world without Krishna. ### confidential knowledge, master, enjoyer
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/D1giBxi2ovc?t=2507
**Verse References:** BG 9
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "I am the master, I am the enjoyer of everyone's activities and sacrifices."
**Summary:** The speaker discusses the most confidential knowledge revealed by Krishna in the 9th chapter of the Bhagavad Gita, emphasizing that Krishna is the master and enjoyer of everything.

This is the origin of ahamkara. This is the important truth Krishna reveals in the 9th chapter of the Bhagavad Gita. In the beginning of the chapter, 9th chapter, Krishna said, idam tu te guhyam pravakshyam anasuyave. Idam tu te guhyam pravakshyam anasuyave. Idam tu te guhyam pravakshyam anasuyave. I am going to tell you the most confidential knowledge. Pravakshyam anasuyave dhyana vigyana sahitam yajnatva mokshase ashubhata. And if you know this truth, you will be freed from all inauspiciousness. What is that truth? Most confidential truth Krishna has revealed in the 9th chapter. There are many aspects of the truth. One of them he is aham hi sarvayagnanam bhogtacha prabhurevaca. This is I am the master, I am the enjoyer of everyone's activities and sacrifices. Natumam abhijananti tatvenathas cavantite. One who don't accept this, I am the master and I am the enjoyer. This is the truth about me. This is the tattva. One who does not accept this. They come to this material world, in this world of illusion. This is the most difficult thing for people to accept. I am not the enjoyer, Krishna is the enjoyer. Or somebody may get an impression, oh Krishna is the enjoyer, I am not the enjoyer. That means Krishna is the enjoyer. And I am what? Sufferer is it? Because opposite of enjoyment is suffering, no? Krishna is the enjoyer. What about me? Krishna is the enjoyer, I am the sufferer. No. By serving him, we will get our enjoyment. That is our pleasure. Not independently trying to be the enjoyer. Krishna is the supreme. The supreme enjoyer. Bhokta cha prabhu revacha. He is the bhokta, he is the prabhu. We must accept. This is the most confidential knowledge that Krishna is describing.

### free will, love, independent desires
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/D1giBxi2ovc?t=2763
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "For love to happen, freedom is required."
**Summary:** The speaker answers a question about free will, explaining that it is necessary for love to exist and that our turning away from Krishna leads to independent desires and entrapment in Maya.

When do we have a free will? And what percentage of free will we are having? Sorry. Why do we have a free will? And what is the percentage of free will we have? Okay, I will answer that. Okay, why do we have free will? See, we were just discussing that we have a relationship with Krishna. And that relationship is loving relationship, bhakti. For love to happen, freedom is required. Just like if I say, I show a gun at you and say, love me or else, you will get scared. I love you. Please let me go. There won't be true love. There is a saying, love cannot come from the barrel of a gun. So, for love, real love to exist, there has to be free will, freedom. So, Jeeva, we have come from Krishna. We are amsa of Krishna. Krishna is fully independent. Swarat. His position. We are amsa. We have small level of independence. We have free will to a small extent. Why Krishna has given that free will to us? Because he wants us to use the free will correctly and love him. But the option exists. If we don't want, we can turn away from him. That is what we are all doing. We have come into this world. Krishna bahirmukha. We have turned away from Krishna. We have come into this material world. Bhogavanchakare. Krishna bahirmukha. Bhogavanchakare. Nikatasta maya. Japati adhare. Very close. When we turn away from Krishna, the first symptom is, we develop independent desires. And moment we develop independent desires, Krishna creates an illusory world. And maya captures us to this world. That is what has happened to us.

---
### free will, human life, illusion
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/D1giBxi2ovc?t=2919

**Content Type:** philosophy

Now, to what extent, what percentage, you said? Okay. All living entities have have have free will. But that free will is most 100% manifest in human life. And in human life, in sattvic life, it is 100% manifest. In rajasic life, may be little lesser. Tamasic life, even lesser. And animal life, even lesser. Plant life, the least. That's why you see plants, they just grow. They stand there. Practically, they have no volition. They don't have an ability. No, I want to be here. Animal, at least they can. No, I don't want to be in this room. I want to go there. They can run around. They are moving living entities. Birds can fly. There is a little bit more expression of freedom. And that expression of freedom is most in human beings. And if somebody is a little more enlightened and he has got a life, tranquil, peaceful life, he is more free. I can do many things. I can plan to do. You see, that's called sattva guna. So, you can see manifestation of free will according to the different forms, life forms. And it is most manifest in human body. And that's why human beings, we can understand all these ultimate truth and come out of this illusory world. Animals don't have that ability to come out of the illusion. They are just stuck in the illusion. We can come out of that illusion with proper knowledge from the shastra, from the acharyas. That is the possibility open to human beings. We will stop here.

### spirit soul, body, eternal nature of the soul
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/8mdZafj-zZs?t=28
**Verse References:** BG 2.20
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers, Newcomers, General public
**Key Quote:** "Krishna teaches that we must understand that there is a body and there is a spirit soul residing in the body."
**Summary:** The speaker explains the fundamental concept of the spirit soul being distinct from the body, drawing from the Bhagavad Gita to emphasize the soul's eternal nature and the body's temporary existence.

But everyone should have a spiritual purpose because we must understand our composition in our present situation. This is the first teaching of the Bhagavad Gita. Krishna teaches that we must understand that there is a body and there is a spirit soul residing in the body. The spirit soul is distinct and different from the body. That is why one day this body can have a heart attack or some other kind of a big disease, and finally I will die. When I die, my body will be lying there. The body that everybody was relating with will be lying there. But then people will say, "Oh, he is gone." Who has gone? What has gone? The spirit has gone. So, there is a dual situation here. There is the body and there is the spirit soul. Because of the presence of the spirit soul, the body is animated. I can sing, I can speak, I can do work, I can think, I can solve problems. All this I can do because of the presence of the spirit soul. When the soul leaves the body, it's a dead body. It is just carried and set on fire into ashes. Nothing more can be done with it when the soul has left the body. But the soul, Krishna teaches, is eternal: na jayate namriyate vā kadācin na hanyate hanyamāne śarīre.

## Doubtless Understanding of Krishna | HG Chanchalapathi Dasa | SB 5 .1.4 | 21.06.2024

### Krishna consciousness, Grihavrata, Doubt
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/8E1xQmrJR0M?t=60

**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "A Grihavrata, one who has taken a vow to execute family duties, has no chance to become Krishna conscious."
**Summary:** King Pariksit expresses his doubt about how someone attached to family can become Krishna conscious, referencing Prahlada Maharaj's statement about Grihavratas.

King Pariksit wondered how a person so attached to wife, children, and home could become so perfectly Krishna conscious. Prahalad Maharaj has said, Matirna Krishne Paratasvatova Mithobi Padhyeta Grihavrata Nam A Grihavrata, one who has taken a vow to execute family duties, has no chance to become Krishna conscious. This is because most Grihavratas are guided by sense gratification and therefore gradually glide down to the darkest regions of material existence. Adanta Ghovir Vishatam Tamisram. How can they possibly become perfect in Krishna consciousness? Maharaj Pariksit asked Shukadeva Goswami to resolve this great doubt.

## Harness Body and Mind Spiritually | Sri Chanchalapathi Dasa | ISKCON Bangalore Sanga
**Speaker:** HG Chanchalapathi Dasa

### mind control, spiritual practice, self-control
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/U6B5gqgV8aQ?t=0
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "As spiritualists, we do not trust our mind."
**Summary:** The lecture emphasizes the importance of controlling the mind and not surrendering to its dictations, highlighting the need for introspection and understanding the forces within the body.

Prabhupada explains that a spiritualist has to be very sober, introspective, thoughtful, grave: vacho vegam, manasa, krodha vegam, jihva vegam, udhara upastha vegam. It means a kind of a force in the body. Prabhupada gives the example, just like our body is designed in such a way, when there is a nature's call, it creates a force, irresistible force. We all have to rush to the washroom. In the same way, there are other forces in this body, and one of them is the force of the mind. As spiritualists, we must know these workings of the mind, workings of the forces in this body, so that we know how to deal with them. Shukadev Goswami is giving one such example. He is saying, "This mind, which is unsteady and which comes with a force, don't trust this mind." This is the first instruction. So, Prabhupada explains, as spiritualists, we do not trust our mind, meaning we do not surrender to the dictations of our mind. The mind comes with a force. Mind comes with an idea: "Let's do this. Let's do that. You do this. You do that." And it comes with a certain force. Don't trust your mind. This is the instruction. Watch the mind's action. So, in other words, this is the instruction. In other words, intelligence is higher than the mind. Soul is higher than the intelligence.

Some time back, one devotee asked me, what if a devotee becomes proud of pridelessness? Yes, it happens. It can happen. We can become proud of many other virtues that a devotee is supposed to have. But, our method of developing all these qualities is not by trying to acquire those qualities separately. We first become devotees of Krishna. To become genuine devotees of Krishna, we have to come to a spiritual platform. Our principle is, in such a person's heart, all divine qualities will come about. If we make an attempt to become prideless on a mental plane, there is a chance that we will become proud of pridelessness. But our attempt is to come to a spiritual platform. States. Prabhupada is in Vrindavan, he has not gone to America but he was already thinking that this should be incorporated in the United States. The name of the society is League of Devotees Inc. I don't know how Srila Prabhupada had figured out Inc, you know that's a practice not in India. And then it says the registered office of the society is situated at Washington USA or at New York USA. So we can see how Srila Prabhupada had even in 1963 October in Radha Damodar temple typing this on his typewriter but envisioning that this society will get incorporated in America. So when this lawyer Goldsmith comes and meets Swamiji, he gives him some of these documents which has the objectives of the society, rules and regulations and all of those kind of things and then he takes that and then he puts it in his office and he understands that and in a way that is suitable for according to American laws and he prepares the documents and once Prabhupada goes to meet the lawyer in his office and a few of these kind of interactions are happening between the lawyer and then according to American law they had to put a board in front of the office for 15 days to see if there is anybody anyone objecting to it or whatever the law leads to.

### God Consciousness, Krishna Consciousness, Rupa Goswami
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/irID2uAh7lY?t=2093
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** story
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers, Newcomers
**Key Quote:** "The lawyer says that Maybe you should call it International Society for God Consciousness because nobody knows Krishna in America. So Swamiji says no God Consciousness is a very vague term and this should be known as Krishna Consciousness and this society will make Krishna known all over the world."
**Summary:** Prabhupada insists on the name 'Krishna Consciousness' over 'God Consciousness,' explaining that the society will make Krishna known worldwide and that the term was inspired by Rupa Goswami.

Maybe you should call it International Society for God Consciousness because nobody knows Krishna in America. So Swamiji says no God Consciousness is a very vague term and this should be known as Krishna Consciousness and this society will make Krishna known all over the world. If people don't know who is Krishna the society will make Krishna known all over the world. That was the kind of reasoning that Prabhupada had that God Consciousness is a very vague word and he used the word Krishna Consciousness and in fact, the word Krishna Consciousness was also coined by Shrila Prabhupada, which later on he would say that he drew that on the basis of one expression that Rupa Goswami had used in one of his works. Krishna Bhakti Rasa Bhavita Matihi. Matihi means consciousness consciousness. Bhavita means imbued with and consciousness, which is imbued with Krishna Bhakti Rasa. So that's how Prabhupada had coined that word Krishna Consciousness and he wanted this to be a society of Krishna Consciousness for devotees to come together, who are practicing and as per the vision of his spiritual instruction of the spiritual master and as per the prophecy of Chaitanya Mahaprabhu. This has to be an international society. And that's how the name International Society for Krishna Consciousness came up.

---

### devotional service, impediments, Vaishnava Aparadha, Krishna consciousness
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/i5ImCRHRxU8?t=126
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "Krishna consciousness is perfect and eternal, and therefore it cannot be lost under any circumstances."
**Summary:** This segment discusses the impediments to devotional service, including Vaishnava Aparadha and the Lord's desire, emphasizing that a devotee advanced in Krishna consciousness cannot be lost.

who has once absorbed his mind in the glories of the Supreme Personality of Godhead may sometimes be influenced by impediments, but he still does not give up his exalted devotional position. According to Srila Vishwanath Chakravarthy Thakura, there are two kinds of impediments to devotional service. The first is an offense at the lotus feet of a Vaishnava. This is called Vaishnava Aparadha. Shri Chaitanya Mahaprabhu warned His devotees not to commit Vaishnava Aparadha, which He described as the mad elephant offense. When a mad elephant enters a beautiful garden, it destroys everything, leaving a barren field. Similarly, the power of Vaishnava Aparadha is so great that even an advanced devotee becomes almost devoid of his spiritual assets if he commits it. Since Krishna consciousness is eternal, it cannot be destroyed altogether, but advancement may be checked for the time being. Thus, Vaishnava Aparadha is one kind of impediment to devotional service. Sometimes, however, the Supreme Personality of Godhead or His devotee desires to impede one's devotional service. For example, Hiranyakashyapu and Hiranyakshya were formerly Jaya and Vijaya, the gatekeepers in Vaikuntha, but by the desire of the Lord, they became His enemies for three lives. Thus, the desire of the Lord is another kind of impediment. But in both cases, the pure devotee once advanced in Krishna consciousness cannot be lost. Following the orders of his superiors, Swayambhuva and Lord Brahma, Priyavrata accepted family life, but this did not mean he lost his position in devotional service. Krishna consciousness is perfect and eternal, and therefore it cannot be lost under any circumstances. Because the material world is full of obstructions to advancement in Krishna consciousness, there may appear to be many impediments, yet Krishna, the Supreme Personality of Godhead, declares in Bhagavad Gita, 9.31 Once one has taken shelter at the lotus feet of the Lord, he cannot be lost. In this verse, the word Shivatamam is very significant. Shivatamam means the most auspicious. The devotional path is so auspicious that a devotee cannot be lost under any circumstances. This is described in the Srimad Bhagavad Gita by the Lord Himself. Parthnaivehanamutra Vinashastasya Vidyavrata My dear Arjuna, for a devotee, there is no question of being lost, either in this life or in the next. In Bhagavad Gita, 6.43, the Lord clearly explains how this is so. Tatratam buddhi samyogam labhate pavarvadehikam yadate chatato bhuyaha samsiddho kuru nandana By the order of the Lord, a perfect devotee sometimes comes to this material world like an ordinary human being. Because of his previous practice, such a perfect devotee naturally becomes a devotee. He becomes attached to devotional service, apparently without cause. Despite all kinds of impediments due to surrounding circumstances, he automatically perseveres in devotional service and gradually advances until he once again becomes perfect. Below Mangal Thakura had been an advanced devotee in his previous life, but in his next life he became greatly fallen and was attached to a prostitute. Suddenly, however, his entire behavior was changed by the words of the very prostitute, who had so much attracted him, and he became a great devotee. In the lives of exalted devotees, there are many such instances, proving that once one has taken to the shelter of the lotus feet of the Lord, he cannot be lost. Kaunteya pratijanihi namey bhaktav pranashyati The fact is, however, that one becomes a devotee when he is completely freed from all reactions to sinful life. As Krishna states in Bhagavad Gita, 7.28, Esham tuantagatam paapam jananam punyakam te dvandhva moha nirmukta bhajan teman dhrdha vrataah Persons who have acted piously in previous lives and in this life, whose sinful actions are completely eradicated and who are freed from the duality of illusion, engage themselves in my service with determination. On the other hand, as Prahlad Maharaj said, Matirna krishne paratas svatova mito bhipadyeta grihavrataana A person who is too attached to materialistic things, family life, home, family, wife, children and so on, cannot develop Krishna consciousness. These apparent contradictions are resolved in the life of a devotee by the grace of the Supreme Lord and therefore a devotee is never bereft of his position on the path of liberation which is described in this verse as Shiva tamam padavim Dasan dhristavak chidantaprabhat So in this chapter of the Srimad Bhagavatam entitled The Activities of Maharaj Priyavrata we just saw Parikshit Maharaj asking different questions about Priyavrata's life how he was a great devotee renounced from all material activities but then he took up he became a grihasta, became a householder had two wives had many children and apparently became attached to family members and he was a ruler, he was a king dealing with all the complications of a king's life how did this happen? because if somebody is attached to family life and such materialistic things he cannot develop Krishna consciousness and if one has become advanced in Krishna consciousness he will not become attached to material things so this looks like Priyavrata's life seems to be a contradiction so that was the question that Parikshit Maharaj has raised and this entire chapter is going to resolve this apparent contradiction and today's verse Shukadev Goswami has begun he is saying bhaada muktam yes what you have said this is what you have said is correct muktam what you have said Parikshit just now bhaadham it is true and then Shukadev Goswami is further elaborating bhagavata utthama shlokasya srimaccharanaravindamakarandharasaaveshita chetasah bhagavata paramahamsadaitakatham it is all describing the position of a devotee bhagavata utthama shlokasya the lord bhagavata bhagavan the lord utthama shlokasya who is glorified by transcendental and eloquent prayers srimaccharanaravinda his lotus feet makharandha the honey or the sweet nectar rasa that is the sweet nectar rasa aveshita chetasaha once whose heart is aveshita absorbed by in the in remembering the lotus feet of the lord which is makharandha rasa bhagavata utparamahamsa and such devotees who are paramahamsas they are liberated daita katham and the lord's activities katham descriptions are daita very very pleasing to them so they are attached to the lotus feet of the lord they are absorbed in hearing the glorification hearing the glories of the lord such devotees kinchit sometimes what happens to them antaraya vihatam sometimes they may be checked by some impediments antaraya vihatam they may be checked by antaraya impediments some obstacles however swam shivatamam padaveem but that padaveem that position shivatamam padaveem that most auspicious position they have attained their own position swam shivatamam padaveem naprayena naprayena hinvanti nahinvanti they never lose that position they never give up that position prayena more or less in that sense almost naprayena hinvanti

### desire, personality of Godhead, enjoyment
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/i5ImCRHRxU8?t=1089
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** General public
**Key Quote:** "The absolute truth is a personality. And what is the meaning of personality? Personality means somebody who has got desires."
**Summary:** This segment explains that the Lord is a personality with desires for enjoyment, which are variegated and multi-dimensional, and that He sometimes arranges for devotees to take on different roles to provide Him with different kinds of pleasure.

Actually, a conscious person, a very primary characteristic of a conscious person, personality is having desires for enjoyment. That's why ultimately Kama Deva means Krishna. Because Kama, desire to enjoy, ultimately belongs to the Lord. He is the ultimate Kama Deva. So He is the Supreme Personality, means He has desires to enjoy. And enjoyment is not one-sided, it is variegated, it is multi-dimensional. And so, Lord, sometimes everyone is praising me. Okay, let me, somebody should also fight with me. That's another nice thing. So the Lord may decide, okay, my dear two devotees, I will impede your devotional service here. You can do another kind of devotional service by going there and taking birth as Asuras. And I will come and fight. And you should be strong. Don't worry. It is a tough fight. Otherwise, what is the use? I come and fight and then suddenly you surrender. It doesn't please me. So I want you to become powerful demons. Shake the whole universe. Then I will come. Then we will have fight. You see how this is? This is actually, Bhagavatam is establishing the personality. The absolute truth is a personality. And what is the meaning of personality? Personality means somebody who has got desires. And he pursues those desires for enjoyment. And the pursuit of the desire for enjoyment constitutes activities. That is actually the Lord and His associates. That's actually the truth.

### material world, spiritual world, perspective, reality
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/i5ImCRHRxU8?t=1223
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** analogy
**Audience:** General public
**Key Quote:** "The greater reality and the dominant reality is the spiritual world. The material world is a small portion."
**Summary:** This segment uses the analogy of a prisoner's perspective to explain how our understanding of the spiritual world is limited by our material existence, emphasizing that the spiritual world is the greater and dominant reality.

What happens is, our view of the world and the creation, it is just like the prisoner's view in a prison in our world. The prisoner is in the prison. He is used to things in the prison. Big walls. He is conditioned. He cannot escape. He cannot relate with the family members. It's all restricted. He wants to enjoy. It's all restricted. So this is actually the perspective of a prisoner. In the same way, our perspective is actually we see from the material world. Actually the truth is, we all know, we all are outside the prison in this world. So we know that how the world is full of irrigatedness. So many activities. There are parks. There are malls. There are restaurants. So many ways to enjoy. By the way, there is one small portion in our city, in every city, called the prison. In the same way, the reality is, the greater reality is, the Lord and His associates and the wonderful pastimes that happen in the spiritual domain. By the way, there is one part of the creation called the material world where all the rebellious living entities are put there. So, this is actually the reality. But, because we are in the material world, we are trying to understand the spiritual reality from the material domain. It's just like the prisoners looking at, oh, there is something called a free world, is it? Oh, there is some park. There are parks there. There are all such beautiful things. Okay, maybe there. So, that's the view of an inmate of a prison. Actually, that's the way we look at when we hear about the spiritual world. But, the greater reality and the dominant reality is the spiritual world.

**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/i5ImCRHRxU8?t=1350
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers

**Summary:** This segment discusses how the Lord's desires and the orders of superiors can lead devotees to take on different roles, using the examples of Jaya and Vijaya and Priyavrata, emphasizing that following the orders of superiors ensures one does not lose their spiritual position.

The material world is a small portion. So, so this is the, so these are the reasons why certain times the Lord wants, Lord is a personality and He has got desires and He wants to pursue those desires for His pleasure and His own devotees take up different roles to give Him different varieties of pleasure and that is another example. So, this is an example Prabhupada has quoted of Jaya and Vijaya where their devotional service was in one sense impeded but actually not in another sense. It was meant for a larger, another kind of a pleasure of the Lord. So, sometimes we may see this kind of an impediment. Another one is Priyavrata himself. Priyavrata was not, his impediment came not from the Lord but from his devotee. Swayambhuva Manu and Brahma, both great personalities, great devotees, they went and told Priyavrata who was in his, like it is described here, Makaranda Rasa, Aveshita Cheta Saha, he was absorbed in transcendental mellows of the Lord but they went and told him, no, no, now you come, become a king, become a householder, have queens, have children, all of that. So, he may do that but Priyavrata when he is doing that, he never lost his shivatamam padaveena prayena hinvanti. They never lose their spiritual position. That is to be appreciated and understood because Krishna consciousness is perfect and it is eternal and it cannot be lost under any circumstance. So here, important point is following the orders of his superiors Swayambhuva Manu and Lord Brahma, Priyavrata accepted family life but this did not mean he lost his position in devotional service. This is the point that this chapter is going to point out. Bhakti is such that if one is in different kinds of roles, if one is in different kinds of situations, but those roles and situations are under the order of the superiors, then one will not lose his devotional position. This is the crux of the matter. shivatamam padaveena prayena hinvanti One will not lose his devotional position if one is under the order of superiors one is acting in this way.

### Vedic literature, acharya, spiritual master, Krishna's representative
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/i5ImCRHRxU8?t=1920
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "You should regard the acharya as good as me... because the spiritual master is dear to the Lord."
**Summary:** This segment explains that the true imports of the Vedic literatures are revealed only to those who have para bhakti to both the Lord and the Guru, and that the acharya should be regarded as good as Krishna because he is dear to the Lord and executes His mission.

This festival is known as Paani Hati Festival because originally it happened in a small village called Paani Hati. This festival is also called Danda Mahotsav. Danda means a punishment, a festival of punishment.

### Yogamaya, Krishna, Surrender, Independence
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/0wGOBQXAnLk?t=60
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers

**Summary:** Discussion of how Krishna is not revealed to everyone due to Yogamaya and the living entities' desire for independence from the Lord.

Contradictory. How can the festival which is joyous be a punishment? How can punishment which is miserable be a festival? So we will see all of that in a short while. Also, this festival conveys a very profound spiritual message. Krishna says, नाहं प्रकाश सर्वस्या योगमाय समावृतः, "I am not revealed to everyone. There is a curtain of Yogamaya that is covering me." So Krishna, who is the supreme personality of God, who is the Param Sathya, who is the Param Tattva, and in this material world, all the living entities are in a spirit of independence from the Lord, don't want to surrender to the Lord, want to lead a life independent of the Lord. To them, the Lord is not revealed easily.

### Krishna Baheermukha Jeeva, Detachment, Dependence on Krishna

Krishna Baheermukha Jeeva. Our position in this material world is Krishna Baheermukha Jeeva. We are Jeeva, but we are Baheermukha, turned away from Krishna. But this is not a natural situation, just like the sunshine cannot hope to be independent of the sun.

### Prakasha Tattva, Balaram, Guru, Revelation of Krishna
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/0wGOBQXAnLk?t=299
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "Krishna is the original person and Balaram is his immediate expansion and he is prakasha tattva."
**Summary:** Explanation of how Balaram, as the Prakasha Tattva, reveals Krishna, and how the guru is a representation of Balaram, giving Krishna to the forgetful living entities; Balaram is Nithyananda Prabhu.

So the living entities who are here in the material world, who have turned away from Krishna, how will they ever be rectified from their illusory, imagined position of being independent of the Lord? So Lord has one immediate expansion tattva called prakasha tattva. The Lord's prakasha tattva's function is to prakasha, to make, to illuminate, to reveal the truth to the living entities, to the living entities who are in ignorance. We are in such an ignorance, just like the sunshine thinking, "I will be independent of the sun," most ridiculous, most impossible. That is our situation. To such ignorant living entities, to bring prakasha, to illuminate them, there is an expansion of the Lord, and that expansion of the Lord is Balaram. So Krishna is the original person, and Balaram is his immediate expansion, and he is prakasha tattva. Krishna is para tattva or bhagavat tattva, non-different. Krishna and Balaram, Krishna and Balaram, both are on the same spiritual absolute position, but Balaram is the one who reveals Krishna, and one who reveals to the living entities about all this is guru, and that guru is actually a representation of Balaram prakasha tattva. This is the understanding. The guru is someone who reveals Krishna. Guru is someone who gives Krishna to the forgetful living entities. So when Krishna came as Chaitanya Mahaprabhu, Balaram, the prakasha tattva of the Lord, came as

### Raghunath Das Goswami, Detachment, Desire for Krishna
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/0wGOBQXAnLk?t=541

by preaching Krishna consciousness. Now, in Chaitanya Leela, there is the great devotee Raghunath Das Goswami. Before he became a Goswami, before he came to that state, he was born into a very rich family in a place called Saptagram, and from a very young age, he had the great opportunity to see Chaitanya Mahaprabhu when he had just taken sanyas. When Chaitanya Mahaprabhu had taken sanyas, and he had a strong desire to come to Chaitanya Mahaprabhu, and he was making an attempt to come to Chaitanya Mahaprabhu, but his family members, father, mother, would not allow him. They thought that, no, our son, because they came from a rich family, they thought their son, our son, should be like us. He should inherit all our property. He should inherit the position that we have, and he should be a normal worldly person. But he did not have any interest in the material activities. He wanted to be with Chaitanya Mahaprabhu, serve the mission of Chaitanya Mahaprabhu. And so he would try to run away from home as a young boy, young man, and his father would send his guards and bring him back. So this happened many, many times, and every time Raghunath Das's father would bring him back. So Raghunath was very unhappy. He was longing to be with Chaitanya Mahaprabhu to serve his mission, be in his association.

### Nithyananda Prabhu, Paanihati, Punishment as Mercy, Chiradahi
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/0wGOBQXAnLk?t=671
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** story
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "Punishment from the lord is very from the master is very desirable because it's a form of mercy of the master."
**Summary:** Raghunath Das meets Nithyananda Prabhu in Panihati, and Nithyananda Prabhu 'punishes' him by asking him to feed all his associates with cheetah dahi, which Raghunath Das happily accepts.

So around that time, near Saptagram, there is a small village, Panihatti. Nithyananda Prabhu had come with a lot of his associates. Nithyananda Prabhu would be travelling around in Bengal broadcasting Krishna consciousness on the order of Chaitanya Mahaprabhu. So he came there, and he would do kirtans, he would tell about Krishna to people, and he had hundreds of associates with him, or thousands of associates with him. So Raghunath Das, when he heard that Nithyananda Prabhu has come to a neighboring village, he came to see him, and from a distance, out of humility, from a distance, he was offering his respects. But Chaitanya Mahaprabhu's associates, sorry, Nithyananda Prabhu's associates pointed out, "Raghunath Das is there far away." So Nithyananda Prabhu wanted to bring him, so they sent message and Raghunath Das was brought. Nithyananda Prabhu was also, he had a sense of a very unique sense of humor, and so when Raghunath Das was brought close to him, Nithyananda Prabhu said, "Raghunath, you are trying to hide from me," and Raghunath said, "No, no, Prabhu, not at all." And then he said, "I want to punish you today." Raghunath Das was very happy. Nithyananda Prabhu is going to punish me. So punishment from the Lord is very, from the master is very desirable because it's a form of mercy of the master. So Nithyananda Prabhu said, "The punishment is, I know you are coming from a very rich family, you feed all my associates, and I have a special request, you should make cheetah dahi, flat rice mixed with yogurt, flat rice mixed with condensed milk, and two parts like this, you should distribute to everybody." So Raghunath Das was very happy

### Chiradahi Festival, Vanabhoj, Chaitanya Mahaprabhu, Kirtan
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/0wGOBQXAnLk?t=817
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** story
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "We belong to the cowherd clan and coming on a picnic like this on the bank of a river and having delicious food to eat is something that we love."
**Summary:** Raghunath Das organizes the Chiradahi festival, serving Nithyananda Prabhu and his associates on the banks of the Ganga, reminiscent of Krishna and Balaram's Vanabhoj pastimes; Chaitanya Mahaprabhu appears mystically.

to accept this punishment. He had all the resources, so he brought all his assistants from his home and got, purchased a lot of cheetah dahi, mixed mangoes to it, mixed bananas to it. Chaitanya Charitamruta says he mixed bananas and honey to all of this and served Nithyananda Prabhu and all the associates on the banks of Ganga. And at that time, Nithyananda Prabhu made a statement, "We belong to the cowherd clan, and coming on a picnic like this on the bank of a river and having delicious food to eat is something that we love." Actually, this statement is significant because Nithyananda Prabhu is Balarama, and Krishna and Balarama and the cowherd boys would go on the banks of Yamuna and they would have their picnic everyday. All the things that their mothers had brought, had sent with them, they would share, called Vanabhoj. So that's what Nithyananda Prabhu was reminiscing. And at that time, Nithyananda Prabhu by his meditation brought Chaitanya Mahaprabhu there, and only a few fortunate souls, it is said, could see Chaitanya and Nithyananda, and there was ecstatic uproarious kirtan with Chaitanya and Nithyananda and chanting of the holy names which filled the air, and this Chiradahi which was given to Nithyananda and Chaitanya Mahaprabhu was served to everyone. So this was a festival, and then towards the end of the festival, mystically Chaitanya Mahaprabhu vanished from the scene and only Nithyananda Prabhu and other associates were there.

### Mercy of Nithyananda Prabhu, Attaining Chaitanya Mahaprabhu, Spiritual Principle
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/0wGOBQXAnLk?t=939
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "If we have to attain the lotus feet of Chaitanya Mahaprabhu service to Chaitanya Mahaprabhu we should get the blessings of Nithyananda Prabhu who is the Prakasha Tattva."
**Summary:** Nithyananda Prabhu blesses Raghunath Das, freeing him from obstacles, and the importance of receiving the mercy of Nithyananda Prabhu to attain Chaitanya Mahaprabhu, mirroring the relationship between Balaram and Krishna.

And the next day, Nithyananda Prabhu was moving away from there to another place, and Raghunath Das once again came and requested him that, "My situation is, I am not able to, my parents are holding me back. I want to be serving Chaitanya Mahaprabhu." And now at that time, Nithyananda Prabhu placed his lotus feet on the head of Raghunath Das who was lying fallen down at his feet, and then Nithyananda Prabhu said, "Very soon you will be freed from all the obstacles," and exactly like that, in a few next few days or weeks, Raghunath Das was able to go and be with Chaitanya Mahaprabhu. So if we have to attain the lotus feet of Chaitanya Mahaprabhu, service to Chaitanya Mahaprabhu, we should get the blessings of Nithyananda Prabhu who is the Prakasha Tattva. So Raghunath Das received the mercy of Nithyananda Prabhu. To receive the mercy of Nithyananda Prabhu, we have to please him. Raghunath Das pleased Nithyananda Prabhu by fulfilling his request to have a big festival of Chitadahi. So this is the principle that we need the mercy of Nithyananda Prabhu to get Chaitanya Mahaprabhu. We need the mercy of Balaram to attain Krishna's lotus feet and Krishna's service.

### Chiradahi Offering, Prayer to Nithyananda Prabhu, Srila Prabhupada, Material Desires
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/0wGOBQXAnLk?t=1037
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** practical
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers, Newcomers

**Summary:** Offering of Chiradahi to Chaitanya and Nithyananda Prabhu, praying for Nithyananda Prabhu's mercy to remove material desires, and glorifying Srila Prabhupada for revealing these truths.

And hence this festival commemorates this important spiritual principle. And so in our temple here on the banks of Kalyani, we offer Chitadahi to Chaitanya and Nithyananda Prabhu, and they will go around in a nauka vihar, and all of us will also receive the prasadam of Chitadahi remembering this past time. Let us pray to Nithyananda Prabhu, by Nithyananda Prabhu's mercy, aarkabe nithai chander karunahave samsaravasana morekabe tuchahave. If we get the mercy of Nithyananda Prabhu, all our samsaravasana, all our material desires which keeps us in this material world will go away. So this is a special festival where we pray to Nithyananda Prabhu to shower his mercy so that all our material desires will go away and we become qualified to go back to the spiritual world. With these few reflections, we will next proceed to the next part of the festival. Shri Nithyananda Prabhu ki jaya! Shri Chaitanya Mahaprabhu ki jaya! Shri Raghunath Das Goswami ki jaya! Shri Chaitanya Mahaprabhu ki jaya! Shri Raghunath Das Goswami ki jaya! Srila Prabhupada who revealed all these things to us, Srila Prabhupada ki jaya!

## Qualifications to understand Bhagavad-gita | Sri Chanchalapathi Dasa
**Speaker:** HG Chanchalapathi Dasa

### devotion, friendship, non-envy, confidential knowledge, qualification
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/MGm-ualXHyE?t=0
**Verse References:** BG 4.3, BG 9.1
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers, Newcomers
**Key Quote:** "So, being a devotee in a transcendental relationship and not being envious of Krishna, these are the qualifications one must have in order to access the confidential knowledge of the Bhagavad Gita."
**Summary:** HG Chanchalapathi Dasa explains that devotion and lack of envy towards Krishna are essential qualifications for understanding the confidential knowledge of the Bhagavad Gita, based on Krishna's statements to Arjuna.

In the fourth chapter, Krishna says, "Bhaktosime Sakacheti Rahasyam Hetaduttamam Arjuna, this is a confidential knowledge, but you can understand because you are my devotee and friend." So, devotion to Krishna in a transcendental relationship, like a friendship relationship, is an important qualification to access that confidential knowledge. Later on, in the ninth chapter, Krishna says, "Idam Tute Guhyatamam Pravakshyamyana Suyave." There also he says, this is very confidential knowledge, but Arjuna, you can understand because you are not envious of me. So, being a devotee in a transcendental relationship and not being envious of Krishna, these are the qualifications one must have.

---

## Srimad Bhagavatam | HG Chanchalapathi Dasa | SB 1.7.34 | 21-02-2016
**Speaker:** HG Chanchalapathi Dasa

### Transcendence, Krishna's nature, Anger of the Lord
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/DgwYgDv6gTw?t=0
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "Because he is absolute, both his anger and pleasure are the same."
**Summary:** The speaker explains that while both Arjuna and Krishna are described as angry, Krishna's anger is transcendental and not subject to material nature.

Both Arjuna and Lord Shri Krishna are described here in an angry mood. But Arjuna's eyes were like balls of red copper, whereas the eyes of the Lord were like lotuses. This means that the angry mood of Arjuna and that of the Lord are not on the same level. The Lord is Transcendence. Please note, Transcendence with a capital T. And thus he is absolute in any stage. His anger is not like the anger of a conditioned living being within the modes of qualitative material nature. Because he is absolute, both his anger and pleasure are the same. His anger is not exhibited in the three modes of material nature. It is only a sign of his bent of mind towards the cause of his devotee. Because that is his transcendental nature. Therefore, even if he is angry, the object of anger is blessed. He is unchanged in all circumstances.

---
### Ashwatthama, Arjuna's anger, Krishna's anger, Srila Prabhupada's purport
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/DgwYgDv6gTw?t=96
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "Srila Prabhupada is taking this as an opportunity to explain that Arjuna's anger was that his eyes were red. Krishna is also angry that his eyes are like lotus."
**Summary:** The speaker discusses the context of Ashwatthama's capture and how Srila Prabhupada uses the situation to explain the difference between Arjuna's and Krishna's anger.

Thus ends the Bhaktivedanta purport. It's a very interesting part of the Bhagavatam. Ashwatthama has been captured by Arjuna. He is Rajva Bhadva. He is being tightly bound by the ropes. Ripum, he is his enemy. Shibiraya Nishantam. And it is Arjuna's intent that he should bring him to the Shibira military camp. Praha, at that time, spoke. Krishna spoke. Praha, Arjuna. And to Arjuna, Prakupitaha. Praha, who is angry. Bhagavan, Ambujekshanaha, Lord, who has lotus eyes, spoke. Praha, because in the next verse we see Lord Krishna speaking. So Bhagavan, Ambujekshanaha, Krishna, who has lotus eyes, spoke. Prakupitaha, to angry Arjuna. And in the purport, Srila Prabhupada has expanded the understanding and he has said that not only Arjuna was angry, even Krishna was angry about the whole thing. If you see the next statement of Krishna, which you will see in your next class, he is telling Arjuna, kill him. Obviously, you can't be telling Krishna to kill him in a very happy way. Kill him. So there is anger even in Krishna's voice. So even Krishna is angry. Arjuna is also angry. Kill him. So that's the kind of... It's not a simple, normal conversation that's going on. So it's full of anger. And so, in the purport, we see how Srila Prabhupada is taking action. Srila Prabhupada is taking this as an opportunity to explain that Arjuna's anger was that his eyes were red. Krishna is also angry that his eyes are like lotus.

---
### Transcendental nature of Krishna, Material nature, Panchabhootas, Kala (time)
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/DgwYgDv6gTw?t=249
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "Krishna's position, Krishna's personality, Krishna's form, Krishna's nature, Krishna's name, Krishna's activities, all of these are transcendental."

That is the difference. Srila Prabhupada takes every opportunity to explain the position of Krishna as a transcendental person. Krishna's position, Krishna's personality, Krishna's form, Krishna's nature, Krishna's name, Krishna's activities, all of these are transcendental. Transcendental meaning, it is something not of this material domain. In the material domain we are familiar with Panchabhootas, right, earth, water, fire, all our bodies, table, all of this is actually transformation of the Panchabhootas. And the Panchabhootas are always undergoing transformation, that is the nature of the Panchabhootas, and they are undergoing transformation under the influence of Kala. So in this material world we see material nature constituting of the Panchabhootas under the influence of Kala undergoing transformations. But Krishna's position is not within the Panchabhootas, not within the Kala, something that is beyond all of this. He is beyond. Whether it is the Rig Veda, whether it is the Upanishad, whether it is the Bhagavad Gita, all of them constantly repeat this

We don't belong to this material domain at all. We belong to another world. Our coming into this world, taking this body made of Panchabhutas, our existence in this Panchabhuta existence of this material domain under Panchabhuta and Kala is itself a dream-like existence. ### general

Om Namo Bhagavate Vasudevaya Reading from Srimad Bhagavatam, Canto 3, Chapter 15, Text No. 31 TABHYAM MISHATSVANI MISHESHU NISHYADHYAMANAM SVARUTTAM AHYAPIHARE PRATIHARA PABHYAM UCHUK SUKHRUTTAM ADHIDRIKSHITA BHANGA ISHA UCHUK SUKHRUTTAM ADHIDRIKSHITA BHANGA ISHA KAMANUJENA SAHASATHA UPAPLU THAKSHAHA Translation and purport by His Divine Grace A. C. Bhaktivedanta Swami Srila Prabhupada When the Kumaras, although by far the fittest persons, were thus forbidden entrance by the two of them, the two chief doorkeepers of Sri Hari, while other divinities looked on, their eyes suddenly turned red because of anger, due to their great eagerness to see their most beloved master, Sri Hari, the personality of Godhead.

---
### renunciation, Krishna consciousness, anger, liberation, sense control
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/HdPMySPtJv4?t=103
**Verse References:** BG 9.22
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "Becoming liberated does not necessitate losing one's sensual activities; sense activities continue even in the liberated stage."
**Summary:** The speaker explains Srila Prabhupada's purport, focusing on the role of a sanyasi, Krishna as the best friend, the nature of anger in liberated souls, and the continuation of sense activities in Krishna consciousness.

Purport by Srila Prabhupada According to the Vedic system, a sanyasi, a person in the renounced order of life, is dressed in saffron-colored garments. This saffron dress is practically a passport for the mendicant and sanyasi to go anywhere. The sanyasi's duty is to enlighten people in Krishna consciousness. Those in the renounced order of life have no other business but preaching the glories and supremacy of the Supreme Personality of Godhead. Therefore, the Vedic sociological conception is that a sanyasi should not be restricted. He is allowed to go anywhere and everywhere he wants, and he is not refused any gift he might demand from a householder. The four Kumaras came to see the Supreme Personality of Godhead, Narayana. The word Suhrtama, best of all friends, is important. As Lord Krishna states in the Bhagavad Gita, He is the best friend of all living entities. suhrtam sarva-bhuta-anam No one can be a greater well-wishing friend to any living entity than the Supreme Personality of Godhead. He is so kindly disposed towards everyone that in spite of our completely forgetting our relationship with the Supreme Lord, He comes Himself. Sometimes personally, as Lord Krishna appeared on this earth, and sometimes as His devotee, as did Lord Chaitanya Mahaprabhu, and sometimes He sends His bona fide devotees to reclaim all the fallen souls. Therefore, He is the greatest well-wishing friend of everyone. And the Kumaras wanted to see Him. The doorkeepers should have known that the four sages had no other business, and therefore to restrict them from entering the palace was not apt. In this verse, it is figuratively stated that the younger brother of desire suddenly appeared in person when the sages were forbidden to see their most beloved personality of Godhead. The younger brother of desire is anger. If one's desire is not fulfilled, the younger brother anger follows. Here we can mark that even great saintly persons like the Kumaras were also angry, but they were not angry for their personal interests. They were angry because they were forbidden to enter the palace to see the personality of Godhead. Therefore, the theory that in the perfectional stage one should not have anger is not supported in this verse. Anger will continue even in the liberated stage. These four mendicant brothers, the Kumaras, were considered liberated persons, but still they were angry because they were restricted in their service to the Lord. The difference between the anger of an ordinary person and that of a liberated person is that an ordinary person becomes angry because his sense desires are not being fulfilled. Whereas a liberated person like the Kumaras becomes angry when restricted in the discharge of duties for serving the Supreme Personality of Godhead. In the previous verse, it has been clearly mentioned that the Kumaras were liberated persons. Vidit Atma Tatva means one who understands the truth of self-realization. One who does not understand the truth of self-realization is called ignorant. But one who understands the self, the super-self, their inter-relation and activities in self-realization is called Vidit Atma Tatva. Although the Kumaras were already liberated persons, they nevertheless became angry. This point is very important. Becoming liberated does not necessitate losing one's sensual activities. Sense activities continue even in the liberated stage. The difference is however that sense activities in liberation are accepted only in connection with Krishna Consciousness. Whereas sense activities in the conditioned stage are enacted for personal sense gratification.

---

So this verse is talking about So we have been reading about the sages trying to enter Vaikuntha and the two doorkeepers stopping them from entering the Vaikuntha Loka. These sages were, it is described here, Suarhatama. They were very, very qualified. They were not some unqualified persons trying to enter Vaikuntha. They were Suarhatama. And still, Nishidhyamanaha, they were forbidden. And when they were forbidden, Animesheshu Mishatsvu, there were many other personalities of the Vaikuntha. Animesha, Animesha refers to unblinking eye. It refers to Vishnu and it refers to Vishnu's associates. So Animesheshu Mishatsvu, they were all other residents of Vaikuntha. They were also watching over this. Nishidhyamana Suhratamahyapi Hare Pratiharapabhyam, Hari's Pratiharapabhyam, His doorkeepers, His associates, Pratiharapabhyam, they stopped them. So the sages began to speak, Uchuhu. From the next verse onwards, Munaya Uchuhu, sages will be speaking. So why were they and how did they speak? They were with angry words they spoke. Kamanujena sahasata upapluthakshaha, upapluthakshaha, their eyes became very agitated. And with what? With the Kama Anujena. Anuja means a younger brother. Kama Anujena refers to a younger brother of desire, Kama. And so Prabhupada has said that figuratively it means the anger. Kamanujena sahasa, suddenly they became angry. And importantly why did they become angry? They were suarhatta maha, they were most qualified. And in the previous verse we saw viditaatma tatvam, they were self-realized. And why did they become angry? That is disclosed in this verse. Because suhrthama didrikshita bhanga, they were didrikshita, very eager to see. They were eager to see whom? suhrthama, their beloved master Lord Hari. And that was bhanga, that was stopped by the two doorkeepers. And hence they became very disturbed. When the Kumaras although by far the fittest persons suarhatta maha api were thus forbidden entrance nishidhyamanaha by the two chief doorkeepers of Sri Hari Hare pratihara pabhyam while other divinities looked on animisheshu mishatsu Their eyes suddenly turned red upaplu thakshaha because of anger kamanujena due to their great eagerness didrikshita to see their most beloved master suhrthama didrikshita bhanga Sri Hari the personality of Godhead.

**Summary:** The speaker elaborates on Prabhupada's points about the Vedic sociological conception, emphasizing the importance of saintly persons (sadhus) in society and their role in disseminating spiritual knowledge.

So Prabhupada has touched upon many important points. The first one is that the sages were not to be forbidden because it is so in the, it is the sanyasi or a mendicant or a sage is permitted to go to any place and no one shall stop them. That is the, what Prabhupada has said here. This is the Vedic sociological conception. How a Vedic society is organized, how the Vedic society conducts is what is being described. Why is it so? Why is it that the sages should be allowed to go anywhere and no one should stop them? Because the sages are carriers of the message of the Lord. They have no interest other than to share the information about the Supreme Lord, the purpose of life and what is that we should do in this human form of life. So they have, they are meant to enlighten the society and hence they should not be stopped. This is the, important position of the sadhus in the Vedic sociological conception. From this we see, the important position given to a saintly person in the Vedic society. He is discharging a very important duty of enlightening the people about the spiritual values of life.

### Vedic society, brahmanas, spiritual knowledge, self-realization
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/HdPMySPtJv4?t=819
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** story
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "Giving knowledge about self-realization is even far superior and more important than becoming a king and ruling over a kingdom."
**Summary:** The speaker uses the example of King Vena to illustrate the elevated position of brahmanas and the importance of spiritual knowledge over material power in Vedic society.

In another place, in the Bhagavatam, King Vena was a very impious king. And then, in the Vedic system, the king has to follow the directions of the brahmanas and rule and encourage and not only maintain the citizens in his kingdom, fulfilling their material needs, he also has an obligation to ensure that their spiritual needs are also fulfilled. But King Vena was not a good king. He was a sinful person and he didn't care for the brahmanas and he was not encouraging any spiritual activities in his kingdom. At that time, all the brahmanas in his kingdom come together and they discuss what is to be done. And they decide that they should kill King Vena. And they kill him. And then, it says, from Vena's body they created another person and made him the king. Now the question comes, if the brahmanas were so powerful that they could kill and dethrone a king, why couldn't they become the king themselves? After dethroning King Vena, because after all he was a bad king. And there Prabhupada explains, no, the brahmanas would not become the king because they had more important duties than becoming a king, which is, they were engaged in self-realization and they were engaged in teaching others in the society in the matter of self-realization. So you see from all of these kind of instructions, where Srila Prabhupada positions that activity of giving knowledge about self-realization is. It's even far superior and more important than becoming a king and ruling over a kingdom. So this is the kind of conception that Srila Prabhupada in all his teachings he brings about, about the role of a saintly person in the human society. And hence in the Vedic conception, such a saintly person should have free access to move around in the human society and give this knowledge to whoever was ready to receive this.

Deha samud bhava They are produced in this body. It's connected with the body. It's not connected with the Dehi. Dehi is the soul. Dehi is the occupant in the Deha. So there is Deha and there is Dehi. And the Deha, Deha samud bhavaha Trigunan The three modes of material nature are associated with the body. Gross body and the subtle body. Whereas Dehi, the soul is not connected with this and he is, he can be situated in a atitya gunan atitya ha stage. Then what happens if we do that? If we come to that stage of being transcendental to the influence of the three modes immediately Krishna gives a wonderful benefit. And one can enjoy immortality. One can enjoy what is deathlessness. In other words one will come to a transcendental state. One will come to a spiritual state when one understands that I am not the body I am a spirit soul and when he is able to understand that he is a spirit soul and nothing can affect that spirit soul. No weapon can destroy. Nothing can touch that spirit. Material things can touch that spirit soul. So janma mrutyu jara all these are things connected with the body and he will be freed from the sufferings. janma mrutyu jara dukkhair vimukto amrutam ashnute So the Supreme Lord Krishna is very concerned about our suffering. He is the Supreme Friend. And he is naturally concerned about our suffering. And hence he has given us a process how we can become freed from that. And we close our eyes to all that become influenced by the rajoguna and tamoguna become greedy in the material world become involved in material activities because of the tamoguna become mad after material things be in illusion be in ignorance and then complain what is this so much suffering Krishna is giving us in this material world? This is not fair. So Krishna has given us a process of becoming enlightened. If we don't take up this process by nature we will be like that especially in Kali Yuga. Kali Yuga things are not at all congenial for spiritual life. So in Kali Yuga the circumstances are arranged in such a way that rajas and tamas influence is very strong. So we have to take up some methods some spiritual process by which we will come out of the influence of rajoguna and tamoguna and then we will strive to come out of these influences come to sattva guna and even beyond guna netana tityatrin dehi deha samudbhavan we can come to that state. And this is what Krishna is teaching.

**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/HdPMySPtJv4?t=2376
**Verse References:** —

### impurity, desire, anger, lust, Vaikuntha, Krishna consciousness
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/LfFYYZdRfuk?t=0
**Verse References:** BG 7.27
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "People should learn Bhagavad Gita and accept the Supreme personality of Godhead Krishna as the Lord of everything, they should practice satisfying the senses of the Supreme Lord instead of trying to satisfy their own senses."
**Summary:** This segment introduces the Srimad Bhagavatam verse and Srila Prabhupada's purport, discussing the causes of falling into the material world and the path back to Vaikuntha through Krishna consciousness.

Reading from Srimad Bhagavatam, Canto 3, Chapter 15, Text number 34. He is stated in Bhagavad Gita, 7th Chapter, Verse 27. It is stated that as long as a living entity is pure, he is in complete harmony with the desires of the Supreme Lord. But as soon as he becomes impure, he is in disharmony with the desires of the Lord. By contamination, he is forced to transfer to this material world, where the living entities have three enemies, namely, desire, anger, and lust. These three enemies force the living entities to continue material existence, and when one is free from them, he is eligible to enter the kingdom of God. One should not, therefore, be angry in the absence of an opportunity for sense gratification, and one should not be lusty to acquire more than necessary. In this verse, it is clearly stated that the two doormen should be sent into the material world, where criminals are allowed to reside. Since the basic principles of criminality are sense gratification, anger, and unnecessary lust, persons conducted by these three enemies of the living entity are never promoted to Vaikunthaloka. People should learn Bhagavad Gita and accept the Supreme Personality of Godhead Krishna as the Lord of everything. They should practice satisfying the senses of the Supreme Lord instead of trying to satisfy their own senses. Training in Krishna consciousness will help one be promoted to Vaikuntha. Thus ends the Bhaktivedanta purport.

institution and if the leaders are playing their role properly and if the devotees are serving the leaders and following the systems and the services that have been assigned then this whole training process will be working and Srila Prabhupada will be pleased and Prabhupada will be blessing the devotees and we will be making progress to go back to the spiritual world

## Srimad Bhagavatam | HG Chanchalapathi Dasa | SB 3.15.35 | 29-01-2016
**Speaker:** HG Chanchalapathi Dasa

### curse, offense, devotee
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/U6_43FQ2sh8?t=0
**Verse References:** SB 3.15.35
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "Although by chance the doormen committed a mistake by checking the brāhmaṇas from entering the gate of Vaikuntha, they were at once aware of the gravity of the curse."
**Summary:** The speaker introduces the verse and explains how the doormen of Vaikuntha reacted to being cursed by the Kumaras, understanding the gravity of offending devotees.

Om Namo Bhagavate Vasudevaya. Reading from Srimad Bhagavatam, Canto 3, Chapter 15, Text No. 35: teṣām itīritaṁ bhāvava dhārya-gōraṁ tam brahma-dandam anivāraṇaṁ astra-pūgaiḥ sadyo hareranu ca rāvuru bhibhyatāstāt pāda-gṛhāva patatārāṁ tāmatikātare nāṁ teṣām itīritaṁ bhāvava dhārya-gōraṁ tam brahma-dandam anivāraṇaṁ Translation and purport by His Divine Grace A. C. Bhaktivedanta Swami Srila Prabhupāda: "When the doormen of Vaikunthaloka, who were certainly devotees of the Lord, found that they were going to be cursed by the brāhmaṇas, they at once became veiled. They were very much afraid and fell down at the feet of the brāhmaṇas in great anxiety, for a brāhmaṇa's curse cannot be counteracted by any kind of weapon. Although by chance the doormen committed a mistake by checking the brāhmaṇas from entering the gate of Vaikuntha, they were at once aware of the gravity of the curse. There are many kinds of offences, but the greatest offence is to offend a devotee of the Lord. Because the doormen were also devotees of the Lord, they were able to understand their mistake and were terrified when the four kumaras were ready to curse them." Thus ends the Bhaktivedanta purport.

---
