**Summary:** The speaker uses the analogy of a goldsmith valuing jewelry to illustrate the importance of understanding the material world from the perspective of enlightened individuals.

So now we should understand, we are all here in this material world, what people of the spiritual world, how they estimate this world. This is a world where people, when they are cursed, they go there. Right? But we think this is a very wonderful place, maybe some things are not alright, we will fix it. In course of time, we will fix it, and we will make it a very good place to live. In, in Indian government language, there is one expression, "punishment posting." If some IAS officer, bureaucrat, they don't cooperate with the politicians, or something, then the politicians will transfer them to Andaman, Nicobar Islands. And that's considered to be a punishment posting. So in the same way, this material world is considered to be a punishment posting for those living entities who are not willing to cooperate and be in harmony with the spiritual atmosphere. If we want to estimate, so in this way, we have to look at how this world is estimated by enlightened sages, or by residents of the spiritual world, how they rate this material world. We get a certain understanding from this verse. Just like if you want to know the value of something, say some ornament, sometimes we, some people drop some, some jewellery in the hundi, and then when we get that jewellery, and we want to make an estimate, how much it is, is it real gold, or some imitation jewellery, somebody dropped, now if you want to make an estimation of that, you have to go to a goldsmith, a goldsmith will check out, and then, because he is an expert in that, he will tell you it's worth how much money. So in the same way, we have to get an estimation of anything, we have to go to a goldsmith. If you go to a blacksmith, and take a piece of jewellery, you are not going to get very good understanding. So in the same way, we have to get an understanding of this, of this world, from those who are enlightened. That is the spirit, that is the perspective.

### desire, karma, knowledge
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/U6_43FQ2sh8?t=824
**Verse References:** BG 4.19
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "In all endeavors, kama sankalpa varjitaha, they have given up the desire for enjoyment, kama, self-enjoyment, or sense gratification."
**Summary:** The speaker explains the concept of 'kama sankalpa varjitaha' from the Bhagavad Gita, highlighting the importance of giving up desires for sense gratification to attain true knowledge.

In all endeavors, sarve samarambha, in all endeavors, kama sankalpa varjitaha, they have given up the desire for enjoyment, kama, self-enjoyment, or sense gratification. Because in every endeavor, a conditioned soul tries to enjoy. What is it that I can get for my sense gratification? Because that's the nature of the conditioned soul, when we come to spiritual life also, in spiritual life also we will be seeing how I can get some sense gratification. So that's the sad part. That is what we have to be watching out. So, yasya sarve samarambha, kama sankalpa varjitaha, so they have given up varjitaha, kama sankalpa, that determination or that desire for kama, varjitaha, jnanagni dhadda karmanam, such people who have become free from desire for sense gratification, in all their endeavors, such people have actually burned their fruitive reactions in the fire of knowledge. Which means, Prabhupada points out very nicely, kama sankalpa varjitaha is a result of being situated in jnana. So, if we are situated in transcendental knowledge, the effect of that is, in all our endeavors, we will not be looking for sense gratification. Conversely, if in all our endeavors we are looking for sense gratification, that is an indication we are not situated in jnana, we are still in ajnana. So, this is what great learned men consider. One is understood to be in full knowledge, whose every act is devoid of desire for sense gratification. He is said by sages to be a worker whose fruitive action is burnt up by the fire of perfect knowledge.

**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/U6_43FQ2sh8?t=1414

**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers, Newcomers

**Summary:** The speaker discusses the gradual development of spiritual knowledge, highlighting the need for qualification and the compassionate role of Lord Buddha in addressing the misuse of Vedic principles.

Some time back, just about 2-3 weeks back, I went to a place, a Buddhist place. And then there was a Buddhist leader and there was a big gathering of Buddhist followers. And then the organizers told us there are 30,000 people here, all Buddhists and following and from all over the world they have come. Then suddenly dawned, I was just reflecting, 30,000 people from all over the world practicing Buddhism seriously. They have come and hearing some discourses and all that. And we understand from the from the parampara knowledge, it is Lord Himself who came as Buddha. Right? And He gave a certain knowledge. But actually that knowledge was, is not the highest knowledge. It was a knowledge that was essential for that particular circumstance. Because people had, were completely misled. And they were not following the real principles of the Vedas. They were completely misled. And so at that time, Buddha came and He had to teach a certain aspect. Because spiritual learning is a very vast learning. And any learning requires qualification. If one does not have the qualification, you cannot learn higher things. Just like if you want in our modern day, if you want to do law, you must be a graduate. And after you have done your graduation, then you can go for law. That's the system. Because you cannot appreciate. Legal things are all very complex. A young mind cannot understand that. One has to grow up a little bit and mature, and then can understand legal complications, why law exists, and all of those kind of things. So in the same way, spiritual knowledge also, there is gradation, and there are very advanced aspects of spiritual understanding. And if you have to understand higher and higher aspects of spiritual understanding, it requires higher qualifications. And the whole Vedic program is to gradually build that qualification in the human society, over many lifetimes, even if it takes many lifetimes. So not understanding all of these things, there was an occasion, there was a situation in our country, in our world, when people had misunderstood. And so at that time, Lord Buddha appeared. Nindasi Yajnavidera Shruti Jatam Shruti Jatam Yajnava Nindasi and he condemned, he rejected. Why? Sadaya Hrudaya Pashugatam Out of sadaya, daya, feeling great compassion for Pashugatam, for the killing of the animals. Animals were being killed, not understanding the real purpose, and why they were killing animals? And when they were questioned, they said Shruti Jatam Yajnava It is the Yajna according to the given in the Shruti, in the Vedic literatures. So they were citing their example. So Buddha said, Nindasi Yajnavidera Shruti Jatam. So it was a temporary arrangement. And then after Buddha, we understand came Shankaracharya. He set right several things. And then came many other Acharyas. So like that, the whole, there was a gradual, and progressive, development of the spiritual thought, spiritual understanding, and that reached its pinnacle, when Chaitanya Mahaprabhu came, Krishna himself came, and gave this knowledge.

### words, mind, senses, devotion
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/U6_43FQ2sh8?t=1807
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** practical
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "Lord Brahma gives in the Bhagavatam, a formula, which, we will never go wrong, with our words, we will never go wrong, with our mind, we will never go wrong, with our senses."
**Summary:** The speaker explains how to avoid mistakes in the material world by controlling our words, mind, and senses through constant devotion to the lotus feet of Hari, following the example of residents of the spiritual world.

And in the material world, we generally act through three things, according to Vedic understanding: by our words, we act. Right? By words we interact in this world, with our mind, and with our senses. And, sometimes, we have all experienced, sometimes we say something and things go wrong, in our relationship, or something happens. And we hurt somebody, and then after that we regret, oh my god, my words were not, I shouldn't have spoken like that. Or some emotions, or some thinking, through our mind also, we may sometimes make a mistake. But we act. And then, or through our senses, we act, knowledge acquiring and active senses. We act, and then we regret, oh I made a mistake, I shouldn't have done that. Right? These are the three ways by which we interact in this material world. And we can make mistakes in this. So, Lord Brahma gives in the Bhagavatam, a formula, which we will never go wrong with our words, we will never go wrong with our mind, we will never go wrong with our senses. And he says, if we follow this, we will be very safe. What is that? na bhārati meṅga mṛśopalakṣyate na bhārati meṅga mṛśopalakṣyate. Bhārati means untruth, or false, or a wrong path. Bhārati, Bhārati, generally refers to Mother Saraswati, right? But in studying Vedic literatures, we must see the context and understand. Here the word Bhārati means one's words. na bhārati meṅga mṛśopalakṣyate. Lord Brahma is saying this to Narada Muni, "My dear, my words never fail. My words never go wrong. My mind never goes into a... My senses will never go astray. How am I ensuring that?" That is by... Here the word used by the... In this verse... Because in my heart... Utkanta means similar sense as... With great anxiety... With great fervor... I am constantly holding on to the lotus feet of Hari. If we hold on to the lotus feet of Hari, with great eagerness, with great zeal... Prabhupada translates that word Utkanta. Utkanta is connected to the word Vaikunta. Vaikunta means free from anxiety. Utkanta means with full... Not exactly anxiety... With full zeal... With a great deal of fervor I am holding on constantly to the lotus feet of Hari in my heart. But because of that... So this is the formula that Lord Brahma is giving, that how we can ensure in our life our words, our mind and our senses don't go astray. And that is by holding on firmly to the lotus feet of Hari all the time. Holding on to the lotus feet of Hari means always living by Harer Anucharaha. In the spiritual world, the residents are all Harer Anucharaha. They're always Anucharaha. They're constantly following the directions of Hari. That is the position of the pure living entity in the spiritual world. So by doing that, even in this material world, which is great calamity around us, we can be very safe. This is the instruction of the Bhagavatam.

### Srimad Bhagavatam, doormen, sages, curse
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/JGJcFBuz4gk?t=43
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** story
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "So, the Lord arrived there."
**Summary:** The lecture begins to explain the Srimad Bhagavatam verse about the doormen, the sages, and the Lord's arrival.

We are reading in the Srimad Bhagavatam, in this part, about the two doormen stopping the sages. And the sages becoming angry, and we just saw in the previous verses, they cursed that they should go down to the earthly planet. And we also saw that the two doormen very graciously accepted the curse that was delivered to them. And in today's verse, we are seeing how the Lord responded when he was aware that this was going on at the seventh gate of his Vaikuntha. evam tadhaiva bhagavan aravindha nabhah svanam vibhudhya sadatikramam arya hridyah tasmin yayo. He arrived there. evam in this way. Thus, tadhaiva bhagavan. At that moment, the Lord appeared there. And the Lord appeared there how? Sahashrihi, along with Lakshmi. So, this verse talks about the Lord at that moment arriving at the scene where the sages and the doormen and all of this cursing and humbly accepting and the sages being angry, all of this is going on. As Prabhupada mentions here, the Lord did not want further aggravation and something more should not happen to his devotees, the doormen. So, the Lord arrived there.

It's a very interesting verse, the verse talks about two things: niraharasya dehinam. One meaning of the word nirahara means not eating food, ahara nirahara, so not eating food, but here niraharasya refers to negative restricting principles, negative principles, don't do this, don't do this. vishaya vinivartante niraharasya dehinam rasavarjam rasopyasya. Here the niraharasya dehinam, one who is abstaining, following all of these negative restrictions, niraharasya dehinam, dehinam, a person who has an embodied person, a living entity, niraharasya dehinam vishaya vinivartante rasavarjam. vishaya vinivartante means he is abstaining from the vishayas, that's what the meaning of niraharasya, he is not supplying the vishaya. vishaya refers to indriyavishaya, so he is abstaining from vishaya, vishaya vinivartante niraharasya dehinam rasavarjam, only vishaya vinivartante rasavarjam, vishaya meaning rasa other than rasa, rasavarjam means apart from the sense of enjoyment, in other words the sense of enjoyment is still there, so he may be niraharasya dehinam vishaya vinivartante, but rasavarjam vishaya vinivartante, he is still attracted to that rasa for enjoying the vishaya is there, other than that, other than that he is abstaining from the vishaya, but rasopyasya paramdrishtva, what is that paramdrishtva nivartante, but when you do paramdrishtva, when you have the transcendental experience, raso api nivartante, even the desire, even the sense of enjoyment goes away. So, it is not that he is only abstaining strictly on the basis of certain principles that no I must not, one he has, one who has developed paramdrishtva rasopyasya paramdrishtva nivartante, so the first point in this verse is

### Vedic literature, transcendental reality, material senses, spiritual learning, faith
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/JGJcFBuz4gk?t=1977
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Newcomers, General public

### Seeing the Lord, Devotion, Meditation, Kumaras
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/4ooHAtaPjas?t=0
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "The Supreme Lord cannot be seen by ordinary eyes But he now became visible to the eyesight of the Kumaras"
**Summary:** The speaker explains that the Supreme Lord is not visible to ordinary eyes but became visible to the Kumaras due to their devotion and meditation.

In this verse we find the word Achakshat Akshavishayam. The Supreme Lord cannot be seen by ordinary eyes, but he now became visible to the eyesight of the Kumaras. Another significant word is Samadhi Bhagyam. Meditators who are very fortunate can see the Vishnu form of the Lord within their hearts by following the yogic process, but to see him face to face is a different matter. This is only possible for pure devotees. The Kumaras, therefore, upon seeing the Lord coming forward with his associates, who were holding an umbrella and a chamara fan, were struck with wonder, and they were seeing the Lord face to face.

### Love of God, Devotional Service, Revelation of the Lord
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/4ooHAtaPjas?t=64
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "That devotees being elevated in love of God Always see Shama Sundara, the Supreme Personality of Godhead Within their hearts But when they are mature The same God is visible before them face to face"
**Summary:** The speaker elaborates on how devotees, through love of God and devotional service, can see the Lord within their hearts and eventually face to face.

It is said in the Brahma Samhita that devotees, being elevated in love of God, always see Shama Sundara, the Supreme Personality of Godhead, within their hearts. But when they are mature, the same God is visible before them face to face. For ordinary persons, the Lord is not visible. However, when one can understand the significance of his holy name, and one engages himself in the devotional service of the Lord, beginning with the tongue by chanting and tasting Prasad, then gradually the Lord reveals himself. Thus the devotee constantly sees the Lord within his heart, and in a more mature stage, one can see the same Lord directly, as we can see everything else.

He is not a Indriyavishaya. But here, Achakshata, Akshavishayam, he, they began to see him. So, Vishnu's position, Krishna's position is, he is not Akshavishaya, he is not a Indriyavishaya. He is not seen, he cannot be accessed by our senses. This is again and again explained in the Vedic literature, Athashree Krishnanamadhi, Nabhavet Grahya Mindriyaihi. Indriyagrahya Nabhavet. Senses cannot access him. He is beyond the senses. He is beyond sense perception. This is what the Vedic literatures have often explained about Krishna's position. ### Analogy of Mobile Phone, International Calls, Limitations of Instruments, Existence of Reality
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/4ooHAtaPjas?t=1168
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** analogy
**Audience:** Congregation / volunteers, Newcomers, General public
**Key Quote:** "Just because our phone, our instruments, cannot reach out, we cannot say such a reality does not exist."
**Summary:** The speaker uses the analogy of a mobile phone unable to make international calls to illustrate that the limitations of our instruments do not negate the existence of a higher reality.

That is the important point. Just like suppose you have a mobile phone. And your mobile phone, you don't have international, you only have facility to make local calls, India calls. You can't make any call outside of India. And somebody comes and tells you, I have a friend in America, and this is the number of my friend. And you use your phone and try to call that number. It's an American number. Call will not go through. You try many times, it will not go through. Now somebody may say, no, no, you charge properly, then it may go through. You can have charge many times, still it will not go through. Somebody may say, no, no, you change your phone version, get a upgrade, a better phone. You can get a better phone, still you try, it will not go through. Go to a place where there is very good signal, and try. You can do anything you want, anything you want, you will not get the call. Then can you say, see, I have tried so much. I don't think you have a friend in America. Or even better, I don't think there is something called America. Because if there is, I must be able to make a phone call and talk. No, it is not so. Just because our phone, our instruments, cannot reach out, we cannot say such a reality does not exist.

### Hamsa Guhyas Prayers, Prajapati Daksha, Purity, Complete Absorption, Experiencing the Lord
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/4ooHAtaPjas?t=1626
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "Only ones whose heart has become completely pure, such people, can be experienced, that Lord, when one is in a state of complete purity, one will be able to experience the Lord."
**Summary:** The speaker discusses the Hamsa Guhyas prayers and emphasizes that only those with pure hearts, in a state of complete absorption, can experience the Lord.

a similar idea is described. Hamsa guhyas prayers were actually spoken by Prajapati Daksha. And generally, Daksha is not considered to be a very exalted person. Of course, he is one, in one sense in the material domain, considered an exalted person because he serves the Lord in his mission of creation of this material world, and populating the world. But still, his prayers are considered very special, and it has become part of the Bhagavatam, because Bhagavatam explains that he did not compose those prayers himself. Already those prayers were there in the Vedic literatures since time immemorial. And so those prayers, which were already present in the Vedic literatures, which he was trained in, so he offered those prayers, and hence, hamsa guhyas prayers have a transcendental significance, and it is part of the Srimad Bhagavatam. So, in this verse, in the hamsa guhyas prayers, Prajapati Daksha says, yaiyate kevalayasva samsthaya, hamsa yatasmai shucisadmane namah. Here again, hamsaya, the Lord's position is completely pure. Hamsa, generally, hamsa in Sanskrit means pure. It also refers to the swan, which is very pure, white, pure. And that's how very exalted persons are called paramahamsas, because they are very very pure. hamsaya tasmai shucisadmane namah. shucisadma, shuchi means pure again, sadma means an abode of purity. Only ones whose heart has become completely pure, such people, sadmane, yaiyate kevalayasva samsthaya, yaiyate, yiyate means to perceive, just like anupashyanti, tatvadarshinaha, seeing the Lord, experiencing the Lord, yaiyate, to experience, to perceive the Lord. kevalayasva samsthaya, again, kevalaya means in a complete absorption, state of complete absorption, swasamsthaya, in his original position, yaiyate, can be experienced, that Lord, hamsaya, shucisadmane, when one is in a state of complete purity, one will be able to experience the Lord.

---
### Vedic Literature Consistency, Ancient Prayers, Padma Purana, Spiritual Saturation, Transcendental Service
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/4ooHAtaPjas?t=1794
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "When our consciousness is saturated, spiritually saturated, in that state, one can perceive. This is the message in the Vedic literatures consistently."
**Summary:** The speaker highlights the consistent message in Vedic literature that spiritual perception requires a consciousness saturated with transcendental service.

So this is the position that the Vedic literatures have consistently presented. Whether it is in the ancient prayers of Hamsa Guhya, whether it is in the prayers of Shukadev Goswami, or it is in the Padma Purana, which Prabhupada often quotes, ata shri krishnanamadhi nabhaved grahyam indriyaihi sevonmukohi jihvadam, jihvadam. In one place in the Bhagavad Gita, when Prabhupada is quoting this verse, Prabhupada translates the words, the words, sevonmukaha, as when one is spiritually saturated with transcendental service. When our consciousness is spiritually saturated, saturated, we understand that when it is completely absorbed, and nothing else is there, remember in chemistry we used to study, concentrated, saturated solution, means it won't, it is fully saturated, nothing else, you can't add any more salt and it won't dissolve anymore, because the solvent is now saturated. In the same way, when our consciousness is saturated, no material conception, no material desires, no material contaminants, no contamination, no anartha, when it is saturated, spiritually saturated, in that state, one can perceive. This is the message in the Vedic literatures consistently.

## Three Dangerous Diversions from Bhakti-yoga | Sri Chanchalapathi Dasa
**Speaker:** HG Chanchalapathi Dasa

### bhakti-yoga, karma, mukti, yogasiddhi, temptation, detachment
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/j8IUXnNznv8?t=0
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** analogy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers, Newcomers
**Key Quote:** "If you are able to somehow resist the temptation of these three exits, then you can head towards the supreme personality of Godhead."
**Summary:** The speaker uses the analogy of an expressway to illustrate how karma, mukti, and yogasiddhi can be diversions from the path of bhakti-yoga.

You're driving on the expressway, you're heading very quickly, but then you see exit, food court, and so you exit, and then you'll see so many different kinds of food all displayed there, and then you get absorbed and lost there, and then you missed the purpose that you were heading in the expressway. So, the shastras point out, when you are trying to advance in the mission of human life, you will encounter three exits. The first exit is called karma. The second exit is called mukti, and the third exit is called yogasiddhi. If you are not careful, you can take that exit, and you can be lost there completely, and forget coming back to the exit. So, you're driving on the expressway, and heading towards the goal that you set out. If you are able to somehow resist the temptation of these three exits, then you can head towards the Supreme Personality of Godhead. Because, if you want to associate with Krishna, you should be free from the temptations of karma, jnana, and yogasiddhi. That is a pure devotee, who only wants to serve Krishna.

---

### rajoguna, enjoyment, sattva, tamas, ignorance
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/bpXAJdRP-d4?t=933
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "The most important thing that Rajoguna does is, it puts us in a framework as I am an enjoyer."
**Summary:** The speaker describes how Rajoguna leads to the desire for enjoyment, often mixed with Sattva Guna (enlightenment) and Tamoguna (ignorance).

The most important thing that Rajoguna does is, it puts us in a framework as I am an enjoyer. So, I am an enjoyer. I must enjoy. Now I have a body. I must enjoy with this body. Sattva Guna creates a certain kind of an understanding. It enlightens. But usually in the material world, Sattva Guna is never alone. It gets mixed with Rajoguna. So, with a certain kind of an enlightened outlook, we try to become enjoyer. And it is not just that, Sattva Guna and Rajoguna mix. There is also always an element of Tamoguna. And Tamoguna's influence is to create ignorance. So, a sense of enlightenment and knowledge and understanding, with the fundamental desire to enjoy, but covered with a certain amount of ignorance.

### knowledge, enjoyment, manipulation, struggle for existence, passion
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/bpXAJdRP-d4?t=1021
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "Intelligence to counteract the hard struggle for existence, is assisted by the senses for acquiring knowledge. And the living energy maintains himself, by manipulating the active organs, like the hands and legs."
**Summary:** This segment explains how knowledge, when combined with the desire to enjoy, leads to manipulating the world for personal gratification, resulting in a struggle for existence driven by passion.

And knowledge, when it is charged with enjoying tendency, we look at this world, and we look at, we develop knowledge about this world, and how to manipulate this world, with our knowledge and understanding, for our enjoyment. You see? That's why Prabhupada says in the purport here, the living condition in material existence, depends more or less on one's intelligence and powerful living energy. Intelligence to counteract the hard struggle for existence, is assisted by the senses for acquiring knowledge. And the living energy maintains himself, by manipulating the active organs, like the hands and legs. But on the whole, the struggle for existence is an exertion of the mode of passion.

Just like the hands, only business is to keep the body in a comfortable situation. We want to have bath, the hands and the legs will work to give bath. We want to dress up, we want to put tilak, hands and legs assist me to put the tilak. We want to eat, hands and legs help. See how hands and legs are parts of the body, they are constantly working for the upkeep and well-being of the whole body. If hands and legs don't cooperate, it is called a diseased condition. We have to go to a doctor, we have to take some treatment, we have to take some treatment. Hand is not working, I am not able to lift my hand, I can't bend, fold my hand. Oh, you have to go to your doctor, you should examine. See hand is not able to work for the whole. Today our material situation is, we are also components, parts of Krishna, but we are the diseased, uncooperative, unwilling to serve the pleasure, for the pleasure of Krishna.

## Who Truly Owns Everything? | Sri Chanchalapathi Dasa @ChanchalapathiDas
**Speaker:** HG Chanchalapathi Dasa

### ownership, belonging, devotion
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/gjUWKTLaLSU?t=0
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers, Newcomers
**Key Quote:** "We must use all of this to serve Rama"
**Summary:** The speaker establishes that everything, including our bodies and strength, belongs to Sri Rama, and we should use them in His service.

I have come into this world, I have this Panchabhuta Sharira, Antribhuta Sharira, Sukshma Sharira. To whom does all this belong? Am I the owner of all this? Am I the owner of this body and the owner of the senses? Am I the owner of myself? To whom do I belong? Oh, we have this body, whatever strength we have, may not be much, but all of this belongs to Sri Rama, and we all belong to Sri Rama. We must use all of this to serve Rama. This is the thinking of a Bhatta. This world belongs to the Lord. Isha Vasya Midam Sarvam. Everything that is there, everything, the Lord is the owner. The Lord is the owner.

## Who is a Paramahamsa? | Sri Chanchalapathi Dasa  @ChanchalapathiDas
**Speaker:** HG Chanchalapathi Dasa

### Paramahamsa, Krishna Bhakti, detachment
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/MVHjpcwTGxY?t=0
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers, Newcomers
**Key Quote:** "Unless one comes to the stage of Paramahamsa, one cannot experience Krishna Bhakti in its full form."
**Summary:** The speaker defines Paramahamsa as a stage of detachment from the material world, necessary for experiencing Krishna Bhakti, and applicable to all individuals regardless of their role in society.

Rishabhadeva, Paramahamsa in Avadhoota Vesha, he appeared. Unless one comes to the stage of Paramahamsa, one cannot experience Krishna Bhakti in its full form. Paramahamsa stage, where you are uncaring for the material world. You don't care for honour, dishonour, pleasure. You are no more searching for pleasure in this material world. Bhagavatam describes Parikshit Maharaj, who was an emperor, was a Paramahamsa. He was in kingly robes. Prabhupada writes, Paramahamsa is required in every field of human activity, because Paramahamsa always thinks, how I can do good for others. But this Paramahamsa Dharma can be practiced in other ways, in Avadhoota Vesha also. Somebody who is a ruler, he should be a Paramahamsa. Somebody who is a businessman, he should be a Paramahamsa. Somebody who is a housewife, she should be a Paramahamsa. Somebody who is a child, a child can also be a Paramahamsa, like Prahalad Dhruvavahar. That should be the goal of human life, to come to the Paramahamsa stage, because in that Paramahamsa stage, one can actually experience...

---

## Who is a Paramahamsa? | Sri Chanchalapathi Dasa @ChanchalapathiDas
**Speaker:** HG Chanchalapathi Dasa

### Paramahamsa, Krishna Bhakti, detachment
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/j0dIFg-thXE?t=0
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers, Newcomers
**Key Quote:** "Unless one comes to the stage of Paramahamsa, one cannot experience Krishna Bhakti in its full form."
**Summary:** The lecture introduces the concept of Paramahamsa, a stage of spiritual development characterized by detachment from the material world and the ability to experience Krishna Bhakti fully, applicable to various roles in life.

Rishabhadeva, Paramahamsa in Avadhoota Vesha, he appeared. Unless one comes to the stage of Paramahamsa, one cannot experience Krishna Bhakti in its full form. Paramahamsa stage, where you are uncaring for the material world. You don't care for honor, dishonor, pleasure. You are no more searching for pleasure in this material world. Bhagavatam describes Parikshit Maharaj, who was an emperor, was a Paramahamsa. He was in kingly robes. Prabhupada writes, Paramahamsa is required in every field of human activity, because Paramahamsa always thinks, how I can do good for others. But this Paramahamsa Dharma can be practiced in other ways, in Avadhoota Vesha also. Somebody who is a ruler, he should be a Paramahamsa. Somebody who is a businessman, he should be a Paramahamsa. Somebody who is a housewife, she should be a Paramahamsa. Somebody who is a child, a child can also be a Paramahamsa, like Prahalad, Dhruvavahar. That should be the goal of human life, to come to the Paramahamsa stage, because in that Paramahamsa stage, one can actually experience...

---
